The Vowed Fast in a Specific Time: Authority of the Vower vs. Right of the Lawgiver
Analysis of the effect of a vow on a specific time's ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a vower's authority (wilaya) is limited to his own right to determine whether a vowed fast can be replaced by another obligation.

Core Idea
A vowed fast makes voluntary impossible, but the time remains usable for other obligations because the vower's authority does not bind the Lawgiver.

When a person vows to fast on a specific day, that day's fast becomes wajib. But what if he then intends a different obligation on that same day? This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami explores the conflict between the vower's authority and the Lawgiver's right. The Hanafi resolution hinges on a key usul distinction: the vower's specification (ta'yin) affects only his own right to treat the time as optional, not the time's inherent capacity to host other obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its default status
Recognize that the act in question is fasting on a specific day, which is initially voluntary (nafl) but becomes obligatory (wajib) due to the vow.
The vow (nadhr) transforms the ruling of the act from mubah to wajib.
2
Note the effect of the vow on the act's description
The passage states that a single act cannot accept two opposite descriptions (voluntary and obligatory). Therefore, after the vow, the fast is no longer voluntary.
This is a logical principle: a thing cannot be both wajib and nafl simultaneously.
3
Distinguish between the vower's right and the Lawgiver's right
The vower's authority (wilaya) is limited to his own right: he can decide that voluntary fasting is no longer legislated for that time. But the Lawgiver's right (haqq sahib al-shar') is that the time remains probable (muhtamil) for any obligation He may have prescribed.
This distinction is crucial: the vower's ta'yin does not bind the Lawgiver.
4
Apply the distinction to the scenario of another intention
If the person fasts that day with the intention of another obligation (e.g., kaffarah or qada), it counts for that obligation. The time remains valid for other obligations because the vower's authority does not override the Lawgiver's right.
The key phrase: 'so the specification is valid regarding what relates to his right... but regarding what relates to the right of the Lawgiver... then not.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هذا الجنس الصوم المنذور في وقت بعينه؛ لأنه لما انقلب بالنذر صوم الوقت واجباً لم يبق نفلاً؛ لأن الواحد لا يقبل وصفين متضادين، فصار واحداً من هذا الوجه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم ومع الخطاء في الوصف. وتوقف مطلق الإمساك على صوم الوقت وهو المنذور، لكنه إذا صامه عن كفارة أو قضاء عليه يقع عما نوى؛ لأن التعين إنما حصل بولاية الناذر، وولايته لاتعدوه، فصح التعين فيما يرجع إلى حقه، وهو أن لا يبقى النفل مشروعا، فأما فيما يرجع إلى حق صاحب الشرع وهو أن لا يبقى الوقت محتملاً لحقه فلا.
And from this category is the vowed fast in a specific time; because when the fast of that time becomes obligatory by the vow, it does not remain voluntary; because a single entity cannot accept two opposite descriptions, so it became one in this respect, so it is hit by the absolute name and with error in the description. And the absolute abstention depends on the time's fast, which is the vowed one, but if he fasts it for expiation or makeup, it falls for what he intended; because the specification only occurred by the authority of the one who vowed, and his authority does not exceed him, so the specification is valid regarding what relates to his right, which is that voluntary is no longer legislated; but regarding what relates to the right of the Lawgiver, which is that the time does not remain probable for His right, then not.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage analyzes the vowed fast in a specific time (like 'I vow to fast next Thursday'). The author argues that the vow makes the fast obligatory, removing its voluntary nature because a thing cannot be both voluntary and obligatory simultaneously. Thus, if one fasts that day with an absolute intention or an erroneous description (e.g., intending it as voluntary), it counts for the vowed fast. However, if one intends another obligatory fast (expiation or makeup), it counts for that other obligation because the specification of the time for the vow is within the vower's authority; it does not prevent the time from being used for another obligation. This differs from Ramadan, which is exclusive.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification of a time for the vowed fast by the vower's choice.
حق صاحب الشرع (haqq sahib al-shar'): The right of the Lawgiver (Allah) regarding the time's potential for any obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect of a vow on a specific time regarding the Lawgiver's right?
A) The time becomes exclusive like Ramadan.
B) The time loses its probability for any obligation.
C) The time remains probable for obligations prescribed by the Lawgiver.
D) The time becomes invalid for any fast.

Key Takeaway
A vow in a specific time does not make that time exclusive; the time remains available for other obligatory fasts because the vower's authority is limited to his own right.

The Effect of the Vow-Maker's Designation on a Vowed Fast
Commentary on the effect of a vow-maker's designation, expanding a usul rule with a qiyas distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that a vow-maker's designation (ta'yeen) renders the vowed act wajib and prevents it from being performed as nafl, and distinguish between the rights of the nadhir and the rights of the Lawgiver in determining the legal capacity of a designated time.

Core Idea
A vowed fast, once designated, becomes wajib and cannot be nafl, but the time retains capacity for other wajib fasts because the designation only affects the nadhir's right.

In this passage from Muntakhab al-Husami, we explore a nuanced ruling about vowed acts in Hanafi jurisprudence. The central question: if someone vows to fast on a specific day, what happens if they fast that day with a general intention or for another obligation? The answer hinges on the concept of 'one from one aspect' (wahid min hadha al-wajh), which limits the effect of the vow-maker's designation to his own right while preserving the time's capacity for other wajib fasts. This lesson will break down the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand 'one from one aspect'
The vowed fast is described as 'one' (wahid) in the sense that it cannot simultaneously be both nafl and wajib. Since the vow imposes wajib, the fast becomes wajib and excludes nafl. But it is 'one only from one aspect,' meaning it may still admit another wajib under a different aspect.
This is a key usul distinction: an act can be unified in one attribute but not in another.
2
Identify the two rights involved
The designation (ta'yeen) is made by the vow-maker (nadhir) and is valid in matters pertaining to his own right, i.e., eliminating the possibility of nafl. However, it does not affect the right of the Lawgiver (Haqq Allah), which is the time's capacity to be used for other wajib acts like expiation or make-up.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the limits of a human's authority in worship.
3
Apply to different intentions
If one fasts the designated day with an absolute (mutaqliq) intention or with a mistaken description, the fast falls on the vowed fast because the time does not admit nafl. If one intends another wajib fast from the night, the fast falls on that other wajib because the time does admit it.
The intention from the night (al-niyyah min al-layl) is necessary for other wajib fasts.
4
Contrast with Ramadan
Ramadan is 'one from all aspects' – it is exclusively for the Ramadan fast. The vowed fast time is not like that; it is 'one from one aspect' only. This is proven by qiyas differentiation.
This contrast sharpens the rule.
5
Summarize the proof (dalil)
The author's proof: the designation occurs by the vow-maker's authority (wilayah), which extends to his own rights (iscat al-nafl) but not to the time's capacity for other divine obligations. Hence, the designation restricts the left of the nadhir, not the right of Allah.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) relying on the nature of authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث في الأمر المقيد اعتبار تعيين الناذر لأنه واحد لا يقبل وصفين متضادين، فصار واحداً من هذا الوجه، فأصيب بمطلق الاسم ومع الخطاء في الوصف. وتوقف مطلق الإمساك على صوم الوقت وهو المنذور، لكنه إذا صامه عن كفارة أو قضاء عليه يقع عما نوى؛ لأن التعين إنما حصل بولاية الناذر، وولايته لاتعدوه، فصح التعين فيما يرجع إلى حقه، وهو أن لا يبقى النفل مشروعا، فأما فيما يرجع إلى حق صاحب الشرع وهو أن لا يبقى الوقت محتملاً لحقه فلا. والحاصل أن الصوم المنذور لما كان واحداً من جهة لم يبق محتملاً للنفل، فإن صامه بمطلق الصوم أو مع الخطأ في الوصف يقع عن المنذور، ولا يقع عن النفل أصلا؛ لأنه لا يحتمله، وأما الواجب الآخر من كفارة أو قضاء فيحتمله صوم الوقت؛ لأنه ليس بواحد من هذا الوجه، بخلاف رمضان فإنه واحد من جميع الوجوه، فإذا كان صوم الوقت يحتمله، فإن نوى من الليل عن واجب آخر يقع صومه عنه لا عن المنذور. وحاصل الدليل الذي أورد عليه المصنّف بقوله: "لأن التعين" الخ هو أن تعين الناذر ذلك اليوم لصوم النذر إنما حصل بولايته، فيصح ذلك التعين فيما له حق من النوافل، فبعد تعينه لا يبقى
The discussion on the restricted command: Consideration of the vow-maker's designation. Because it is one and does not accept two contradictory descriptions, so it became one from this aspect. So it is hit by the absolute name and with error in the description. And the absolute abstention is suspended on the fast of the time which is the vowed (fast), but if he fasts it for an expiation or a make-up, it falls upon what he intended; because the designation occurred only by the authority of the vow-maker, and his authority does not extend beyond him. So the designation is valid in what pertains to his right, which is that the supererogatory does not remain permissible. As for what pertains to the right of the Lawgiver, which is that the time does not remain probable for His right, then it is not (valid). The summary is that the vowed fast, since it is one from one aspect, remains not probable for supererogatory; so if he fasts it with the absolute fast or with error in the description, it falls upon the vowed (fast) and does not fall upon the supererogatory at all, because it does not admit it. As for another obligatory (fast) like expiation or make-up, the time-fast admits it, because it is not one from this aspect, unlike Ramadan which is one from all aspects. So if the time-fast admits it, then if he intended from the night for another obligatory (fast), his fast falls upon it, not upon the vowed (fast). The gist of the proof that the author presented by his saying 'because the designation' is that the designation by the vow-maker of that day for the vowed fast occurred only by his authority, and that designation is valid in what pertains to his right from supererogatory acts, so after his designation it does not remain
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage from Muntakhab al-Husami is a commentary on a matn discussing the effect of a vow-maker's designation of a specific day for a vowed fast. The passage type is a ruling with rational proof. The key point is that the vowed fast, once designated, becomes 'one' in the sense that it cannot be both supererogatory (nafl) and obligatory (wajib) simultaneously; it necessarily becomes wajib. Therefore, if someone fasts that day without specifically intending the vow, or even intending something else like another wajib fast, the fast will be counted for the vow if the intention was general, but if he intended another specific wajib fast from the night, it will count for that other wajib, not the vow. This is because the time after designation is not capable of being nafl, but it is capable of being another wajib (like expiation or make-up), unlike Ramadan where the time is exclusively for Ramadan. The commentator then summarizes the proof: the vow-maker's designation is valid only in matters pertaining to his own right (i.e., eliminating nafl), but it does not affect the right of the Lawgiver (i.e., the time's capacity for other obligations). All examples are from Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yeen): The act of the vow-maker designating a specific day or time for the vowed fast
ناذر (nadhir): The person who makes a vow (nadhara) to perform a specific act of worship, here a fast
وصفين متضادين (wasfayn mutadadayn): Two contradictory attributes, here nafl and wajib, which cannot coexist in the same act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The fast counts for the make-up, not the vow.
B) The fast counts for the vow, not the make-up.
C) The fast is invalid because two intentions conflict.
D) The fast counts as both.

Key Takeaway
The vow-maker's designation eliminates the possibility of nafl but does not prevent the time from being used for other wajib fasts, because the designation is limited to the nadhir's right.

The Problematically Extensive Time (al-Waqt al-Mushkil) and Hajj
Expanding the concept of al-waqt al-mushkil via the Hajj example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third type of time-bound obligation (mu'qqat bi-waqtin mushkil) and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the timing of Hajj performance.

Core Idea
Hajj's time is both a container and a measure, causing an ikhtilaf on whether delay is allowed.

This lesson examines a unique category of time-bound obligations in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: those with a problematically extensive time (mu'qqat bi-waqtin mushkil). Hajj serves as the paradigmatic example. Understanding this category requires distinguishing between time as a container (zarf) and time as a measure (mi'yar). We will explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on whether Hajj must be performed in the first available year or can be delayed, and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that Hajj is an obligation with a time that is both extensive (lifetime) and specific (months of Hajj), creating a problematic combination.
This is the third type of time-bound obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf
Contrast Imam Muhammad's view (tawsi'ah: can delay) with Abu Yusuf's view (tadyiq: must perform in first year).
Both agree on the condition that it must be performed before death.
3
Analyze the basis
See that the ikhtilaf centers on whether precaution demands immediate performance or the extensive time allows delay.
Muhammad focuses on the time being extensive; Abu Yusuf on avoiding the risk of missing.
4
Determine the effect
The dispute only affects the issue of sin (ithm); the later Hajj counts as ada' (on time) and supererogatory remains valid.
There is no disagreement on the validity or timing category of the performed Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث في الأمر المقيد المؤقت بوقت مشکل توسعه وهو الحج، فإنه فرض العمر، ووقته أشهر الحج وحياته مدة يفضل بعضها لحجة أخرى مشكل، ومن حكمه أن عند محمد يسعه التأخير لكن بشرط أن لايفوته في عمره، وعند أبي يوسف محله يتعين عليه الأداء في أشهر الحج من العام الأول احتياطاً احترازاً عن الفوات، فظهر ذلك في حق المأثم لا غير حتى يبقى النفل مشروعاً. وجوازه عند الإطلاق بدلالة تعين من المؤدي؛ إذ الظاهر أنه لا يقصد النفل، وعليه حجة الإسلام..
The inquiry into the restricted command that is time-bound with a problematically extensive time, and that is Hajj, for it is an obligation of a lifetime, and its time is the months of Hajj and his lifespan is a period in which some of it is preferred for another Hajj, problematic. And among its rulings is that according to Muhammad he may delay it, but on condition that he does not miss it in his lifetime. According to Abu Yusuf, it is determined upon him to perform it in the months of Hajj of the first year as a precaution to avoid missing it. So that effect appears only in the matter of sin, so that supererogatory remains valid. And its permissibility when the intention is absolute is by the indication of determination from the performer, for the apparent is that he does not intend supererogatory while he owes the obligatory Hajj.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding the third type of time-bound obligation: that which has a problematically extensive time, exemplified by Hajj. The author explains that Hajj is obligatory once in a lifetime, and its time is both the specific months of Hajj and the entire lifetime, creating a problematic mix of being a container (like prayer time) and a measure (like fasting time). The key dispute is between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf: Muhammad allows delaying Hajj beyond the first year as long as it is performed before death, while Abu Yusuf requires performance in the first year to avoid the risk of missing it. The effect of this disagreement is only in terms of sin: according to Abu Yusuf, delaying beyond the first year makes one sinful (fasiq), while Muhammad says no sin until death approaches. Both agree that if one delays, the later performance counts as ada' (not qada'). Additionally, if one intends Hajj in absolute terms without specifying fard or nafil, it suffices for the fard due to the circumstantial indication that a Muslim who has not yet performed the obligatory Hajj would not intend nafil. The Shafi'i opinion that the nafil intention is invalid is rejected.

Key Terms
مؤقت بوقت مشكل (mu'qqat bi-waqtin mushkil): A time-bound obligation whose time is problematically extensive, combining aspects of a container (ظرف) and a measure (معيار).
توسعة (tawsi'ah): The view that the obligation can be performed at any time within the extensive period, not restricted to the earliest possible opportunity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what practical effect does the ikhtilaf between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf have on a person who delays Hajj beyond the first year?
A) He becomes sinful according to Abu Yusuf until he performs it
B) He becomes sinful according to Muhammad if he delays
C) His Hajj becomes qada' if performed after the first year
D) He must perform Hajj again if he delays beyond the first year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of time-bound obligations reveals that Hajj's extensive time allows delay, with the ikhtilaf confined to the issue of sin.

Ada' and Qada': The Two Modes of Fulfilling a Wajib
Defining ada' and qada' as categories of fulfilling a wajib command.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of ada' and qada', distinguish between them, and apply the definitions to categorize the performance of a wajib act.

Core Idea
Ada' delivers the exact wajib; qada' discharges by a like — both fulfill the obligation.

This lesson unpacks the two fundamental categories of fulfilling a wajib command in Hanafi usul: ada' (performance in time) and qada' (makeup later). The passage defines each with precise grammatical analysis, showing how the cause and the recipient are connected. Understanding these definitions is essential for correctly classifying any act of worship or obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
The passage states that the fulfillment of a wajib command is of two types: ada' and qada'. Recognize that every wajib must be performed either as ada' (on time) or qada' (later).
These are the only two modes; there is no third.
2
Parse the definition of ada'
Ada' is defined as 'delivering the exact wajib by its cause to its due recipient'. Break this down: the act must be the precise wajib (not a substitute), it must be triggered by a cause (e.g., time for prayer), and it must be directed to the proper recipient (e.g., Allah).
The ba' in 'biasababihi' indicates causality; 'ila' indicates the recipient.
3
Parse the definition of qada'
Qada' is defined as 'discharging the wajib by a like from the one who has it as his right'. Here the emphasized element is 'mithl' (like): the makeup act must be similar to the original wajib, not any substitute.
The ba' in 'bimithlin' is attached to 'isqat' (discharging).
4
Note the grammatical pointers
The author clarifies that 'biasababihi' relates causality to the wajib, and 'ila mustahaqqihi' directs the delivery. For qada', 'min indihi' indicates the obligated person himself performs the substitute.
These grammatical points solidify the intended meaning.
5
Apply the definitions
Given a scenario where a wajib act is performed, determine whether it counts as ada' or qada' based on timing and whether it is the exact act or a substitute.
Use the criteria: exact vs. like, within time vs. later.

Source Text

Section on the ruling of the obligatory by command. It is of two types: ada' (performance) which is delivering the exact wajib by its cause to its due recipient, and qada' (makeup) which is discharging the wajib by the like from the one who has it as his right. 'By its cause to its due recipient' – the ba' is for causality, it relates to the wajib, and 'ila' relates to delivering, the pronoun in 'biasababihi' refers to the wajib, and in 'mustahiqqihi' to the wajib. That is, ada' is delivering the same wajib established in the dhimmah by the cause that necessitates it, like time for prayer and the month for fasting, to the one who deserves that wajib. This definition includes the delivery of time-bound obligations in their time like prayer and fasting, and non-time-bound like zakat and fitr charity. What is meant by delivery is bringing forth from existence to non-existence at the specified time for it, otherwise actions are accidents that cannot be delivered. 'By the like from the one who has it as his right' – the ba' is attached to discharging, meaning qada' is discharging what is in the dhimmah by the like from the one who has it, i.e., by delivering the wajib from the obligated person that is his right, meaning that wajib was the right of the absolute, and it became obligatory.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the two categories of fulfilling a wajib command: ada' and qada'. The author defines ada' as delivering the exact wajib (like prayer itself) by the cause (like time) to the one who deserves it (like Allah). Qada' is defined as discharging the obligation by a like substitute, i.e., performing a similar act later. The commentary clarifies the grammatical relationships: the ba' in 'biasababihi' indicates causality, and the preposition 'ila' indicates the recipient. The definition of ada' is comprehensive: it applies to time-bound obligations like prayer and fasting when performed in their proper time, and to non-time-bound obligations like zakat. Delivery is explained metaphorically as bringing the act from potential to actuality, since actions are not physical objects. For qada', the 'like' means a similar act performed by the obligated person, and it is his 'right' because he owes it.

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): The delivery of the exact wajib act by its cause to its due recipient, performed in the proper time or at the first opportunity.
قضاء (qaḍā'): The discharge of a wajib from the dhimmah by performing a similar act (mithl) at a later time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in this passage, how is 'ada'' different from 'qada''?
A) Ada' delivers the exact wajib by its cause; qada' discharges by a similar act
B) Ada' is only for time-bound obligations; qada' for non-time-bound
C) Ada' requires intention; qada' does not
D) Ada' is performed on time; qada' is always sinful

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, ada' is the primary fulfillment of a wajib by its exact self, while qada' is a secondary fulfillment by a like substitute when the original is missed.

Hanafi Definitions of Ada' and Qada'
Definition and dispute on fulfillment of wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada' and qada' according to the Hanafi school, distinguish them, and apply the definitions to the case of intention in Hajj.

Core Idea
Ada' is delivering the wajib by its cause; qada' is discharging it with a substitute from oneself.

In this passage, the author delineates the two modes of fulfilling a wajib: performance (ada') and make-up (qada'). Understanding these definitions is foundational for determining when an obligation is discharged. The passage also applies these concepts to a disputed scenario involving intention in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Terms and Definitions
Read the Arabic definitions of ada' and qada'. Note the key components: 'ayn al-wajib, sabab, mustahaqq, mithl.
The definition of ada' includes 'bi sababihi', emphasizing the cause.
2
Analyze the Grammatical Structure
Examine the prepositions: 'bi sababihi' (by its cause) indicates causation; 'ila mustahaqqihi' (to its entitled recipient) indicates delivery. Understand how each element contributes to the definition.
The ba' in 'bi sababihi' is for causation, and 'ila' indicates direction.
3
Examine the Application to Hajj
Consider the hypothetical: a person intends a supererogatory Hajj while the obligatory Hajj is still due. According to an opinion narrated from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf, the supererogatory intention is valid and the fard remains owed. How does the definition of ada' support this?
The time is capable of accommodating both fard and nafl, similar to prayer times.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
Al-Shafi'i holds that the intention of nafl is void and the Hajj falls for the fard. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence): the Hanafi position allows the nafl reward while the obligation remains; the Shafi'i position discharges the obligation immediately.
The difference stems from how each school views the effect of determination on alternative intentions.
5
Classify the Types of Wajib
The passage also discusses types of time-bound obligations: time as a cause vs. time as a measure. Understand where qada' fits: it is not time-bound but absolute, yet still requires a similar act.
The author distinguishes between time-bound (muwaqqat) and non-time-bound obligations.

Commentary
This passage begins by defining the two categories of fulfilling a wajib (obligation) that arises from a command (amr). The author delineates ada' (performance) as the delivery of the exact wajib (e.g., the specific prayer or fasting) by its cause (sabab, such as time) to its rightful recipient (e.g., Allah). Qada' (make-up) is defined as the discharge of the wajib by performing a similar act from oneself, meaning the obligated person offers a substitute after the original time or opportunity has passed, and it is considered his right (i.e., the duty returns to him). A long commentary then follows, explaining nuances: a disagreement about the effect of intention when one has both a supererogatory and obligatory Hajj. Abu Hanifa (via Abu Yusuf) holds that if one intends a supererogatory Hajj while the obligatory Hajj is due, the intention is valid for nafl because the time accommodates both, but the fard remains. Shafi'i holds the nafl intention is void and it counts for fard. The passage then clarifies that when intention is absolute (not specifying fard or nafl), the state of the person indicates the obligatory intent. The commentary also discusses classification of time in relation to obligations, distinguishing between time as a cause (sabab) and time as a mere measure (mi'yar). The definitions of ada' and qada' are further refined with examples and grammatical analysis.

Key Terms
أداء (ada'): تسليم عين الواجب بسببه إلى مستحقه (delivering the exact wajib by its cause to its entitled recipient)
قضاء (qada'): إسقاط الواجب بمثل من عنده (discharging the wajib with a similar act from oneself)

Categories of Adā' and Qadā' with Usul Principles
Explains types of adā'/qadā' with usul principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that non-rational acts (ghayr ma'qūl) are not extended by qiyas, and distinguish between adā' (performance) and qadā' (substitute) in divine and human rights using examples from sacrifice, prayer, and transactions.

Core Idea
Non-rational acts like sacrifice are not extendable by qiyas; time-bound obligations revert to original rules after expiry.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text delves into the categories of adā' (performance) and qadā' (substitute) across divine and human rights. It uses the example of sacrifice (udhiya) to illustrate that acts not rationally understood cannot be extended by qiyas. Instead, after the time limit passes, the ruling returns to the original principle—charity. The same logic applies to takbīrāt in Eid prayer for a latecomer and to returning usurped property. You will explore how the Hanafi school employs istihsan and caution to resolve apparent conflicts between obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core usul principle
Read the discussion on sacrifice (udhiya). Note that the author argues charity after the days of sacrifice is not based on qiyas to sacrifice itself, but on a return to the original principle of charity, because sacrifice is not rationally understood (ghayr ma'qūla).
This principle is key: acts that are purely devotional (ta'abbudi) cannot be analogized.
2
Analyze the takbīrāt dispute
Examine the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the majority Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) regarding a person who joins the Imam in ruku' during Eid prayer. Abu Yusuf says he does not say the takbīrāt because they are missed from their proper place; the Hanafi school says he says them in ruku' because ruku' resembles standing.
This illustrates how resemblance (shabah) can prevent an obligation from being considered 'missed'.
3
Distinguish between adā' kāmil and qāṣir
Look at the example of returning a usurped slave. If returned in the same condition, it is adā' kāmil (complete performance); if returned with a debt or crime attached, it is adā' qāṣir (deficient performance). Understand that deficiency in description does not nullify the performance but reduces its perfection.
This mirrors the divine rights examples: praying in congregation vs. alone.
4
Compare with dower (mahr) example
Consider a husband who gives a slave owned by another as dower, then buys and delivers it. This is considered adā' (performance) because he delivers what was contracted, but it also resembles qadā' because he acquires ownership only before delivery. This shows overlapping categories.
The wife is forced to accept this as performance, even though it is partially substitute.
5
Synthesize the categories in human rights
The passage states that all seven categories of adā' and qadā' apply to human rights. Map each divine rights example to a human rights counterpart, such as prayer in congregation (complete) vs. alone (deficient), and note the practical consequences for liability.
For example, if the usurped slave perishes after return, the usurer is free if the return was complete, but may be liable if deficient.

التضحية، حيث قلتم وجب عليه أن يتصدق بعين الشاة أو بالقيمة بعد أيام النحر . تقرير الجواب: أنا لا نجعل التصدّق بعين الشاة أو بالقيمة واجبات باعتبار قيامه مقام التضحية، حتى يلزم الزمتم بل للاحتياط باعتبار أن تكون التضحية في أيامها فرعاً، ويكون التصدّق بعين الشاة أو بالقيمة أصلاً وتكون هي قائمة مقامه بعارض الضيافة؛ لأن الناس في تلك الأيام أضياف الله ومن عادة الكريم أن يضيف بأطيب الطعام عنده، وهوا للحم المزكي المراق منه الدم، ولذا قلنا بالتضحية في تلك الأيام، فإذا مضت تلك الأيام رجعنا إلى ما هو الأصل، وهو التصدق بالعين أو بالقيمة؛ إذ هو المشروع في باب المال، وإنما قلنا باعتبار احتمال قيام التضحية مقام التصدق؛ لأن التضحية في أيامها تحتمل أن تكون أصلا بنفسها، وتحتمل أن تكون خلفاً، والأصل هو التصدق، فما دامت الأيام موجودة رجّحنا الاحتمال الأول، وقلنا بوجوب التضحية، وبعد الأيام رجّحنا الاحتمال الأخير، وقلنا بوجوب التصدّق. ولهذا أي لأجل أن ما لا يعقل مثله لا قضاء له، كما يفهم من الإيراد التزاماً. فيمن أدرك الإمام إلخ يعنى من أدرك الإمام في صلاة العيد في الركوع ويعلم أن الإمام يرفع رأسه لو أشغل بالتكبيرات قائماً فله أن يدخل في الركوع مع الإمام، ولا يقضي التكبيرات في الركوع عند أبي يوسف الله، لأنها فاتت عن موضعها وهو القيام، وهو غير قادر على مثل من عنده قربة في الركوع، فلا يصح قضاؤها فيه كالقراءة والقنوت، وعندنا يكبر في الركوع من غير رفع يد؛ لأن الركوع فرض والتكبيرات واجبة فيراعي لكنا نقول بأن الركوع يشبه القيام فباعتبار هذه الشبهة لايتحقق الفوات، فيؤتى أي المشابهة بها في الركوع احتياطاً. وهذه الأقسام كلها تتحقق في حقوق العباد، فتسليم عين العبد المغصوب أداء كامل ورده مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بسبب كان في يد الغاصب أداء قاصر. وإذا أمهر عبد الغير ثم اشتراه كان تسليمه أداء حتى تجبر على القبول، أي المرأة وشبيها بالقضاء من حيث إنه مملوكه قبل التسليم حتى ينفذ إعتاقه فيه دون إعتاقها، : : = حالهما حتى الإمكان، فرفع اليدين في التكبيرات سنة، وكذا وضعهما على الركبتين في الركوع سنة، فلا يترك أحدهما بالآخر، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي هو شبيه بالأداء؛ لأن هذا قضاء من حيث الذات؛ لأن محلّها القيام قبل الركوع وقد فات لكنه شبيه بالأداء كما بينه المصنف. يشبه القيام لقيام النصف الأسفل على حاله، ولأن من أدرك الإمام في الركوع فقد أدرك الركعة بجميع أجزائها من القيام والقراءة تقديراً. ولما فرغ من بيان أنواع الأداء والقضاء في حقوق الله تعالى شرع في بيان أنواعهما في حقوق العباد. وهذه الأقسام السبعة المذكورة من الأداء والقضاء. كلها تتحقق إلخ أيضا كما تتحقق في حقوق الله تعالى. العبد المغصوب على الوصف الذي ورد عليه الغصب. أداء كامل لأنه أداء كما غصب من الأصل والوصف، فكان كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة في حقوق الله تعالى. ورده مشغولاً إلخ: يعنى ردّ العبد المغصوب مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بأن استهلك العبد مال إنسان حال كونه في يد الغاصب فتعلّق برقبته الدين، أو جنى جناية يستحق بها رقبته أو طرفه حال كونه في يد الغاصب، فردّ ذلك العبد أداء قاصر، أما كونه أداء فظاهر لرد ذلك العبد الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وأما كونه قاصراً فلقصور في الوصف حيث ردّه على غير الوصف الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وصار كأداء الصلاة منفرداً، فلو هلك ذلك العبد في يد المالك قبل الدفع إلى ولي الجناية، أو البيع في الدين برئ الغاصب لوجود أصل الأداء، ولو دفع إلى ولي الجناية أو قتل فيها، أو بيع في ذلك الدين المالك على الغاصب بقيمة العبد لقصور في الأداء، فكأنه لم يوجد. رجع تسليمه إلى الزوجة في المهر أداء وشبيها بالقضاء إلخ: هذا نظير للأداء الشبيه بالقضاء. وحاصله إذا تزوج الرجل بامرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً معيّنا مملوكا لغيره، ثم اشترى ذلك العبد وسلّمه إلى زوجته كان ذلك أداء، حيث سلّم ما وقع عليه العقد حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول ذلك العبد الممهور، وهذا من علامة كونه أداء وشبيها بالقضاء؛ =
Statement of the description of the ruling of the command: it suffices, if Allah wills, as if the heir voluntarily performs it in fasting, and we do not obligate charity in making up [the sacrifice] with the sheep or with the value based on it standing in place of the sacrifice, rather we consider the probability of the sacrifice standing in the place of charity originally because it is what is legislated in the chapter of wealth, and for this reason it is not returned to the like with the return of time, and for this reason Abu Yusuf said regarding one who catches the Imam in the Eid prayer in ruku': he does not say the takbir because he is not capable of a like of what he has from himself as an act of drawing near, if Allah wills. And analogical issues are never connected to the will. In fasting without bequest, we hope for acceptance from him if Allah wills, so also here. His statement 'and we do not obligate charity' etc. is an answer to another objection presented to him: its explanation: that sacrifice (which is the spilling of blood during the days of slaughter) is known as an act of drawing near by textual proof, and it is not rationally understood because it is destroying the animal and causing it pain, so it is not permissible to analogize others to it and make others stand in its place by way of extension. And you make charity of the actual sheep (when the sheep designated for sacrifice by vow or by purchase from the poor person with intention of sacrifice remains after the days of slaughter, or the value when the sheep designated for sacrifice by vow or otherwise is consumed, or the one upon whom it was obligatory did not sacrifice until the days of slaughter passed) stand in the place of sacrifice, when you said it is obligatory upon him to give charity of the actual sheep or the value after the days of slaughter. The explanation of the answer: we do not make charity of the actual sheep or the value obligatory based on its standing in the place of sacrifice, so that you would be required, rather it is out of caution, considering that sacrifice during its days is a branch, and charity of the actual sheep or the value is the original, and it stands in its place due to the incident of hospitality; because the people in those days are the guests of Allah, and it is the habit of the generous to host with the best food he has, and it is the meat of the legally slaughtered animal from which blood is drained. Therefore we said sacrifice is obligatory in those days. When those days pass, we return to what is the original, which is charity of the actual or the value, because it is what is legislated in the chapter of wealth. And we only said based on the probability of sacrifice standing in the place of charity because sacrifice during its days possibly is an original itself, and possibly is a substitute, and the original is charity. As long as the days exist, we prefer the first probability and say obligation of sacrifice. After the days, we prefer the latter probability and say obligation of charity. And for this reason, i.e., because what is not rationally similar to it has no substitute, as understood from the objection implicitly. Regarding one who catches the Imam etc., meaning one who catches the Imam in the Eid prayer in ruku' and knows that the Imam will raise his head if he occupies himself with the takbirs while standing, he may enter into ruku' with the Imam, and he does not make up the takbirs in ruku' according to Abu Yusuf, because they were missed from their place which is standing, and he is not capable of a like of what he has from himself as an act of drawing near in ruku', so making them up in it is not valid like recitation and qunut. According to us, he says takbir in ruku' without raising hands, because ruku' is obligatory and the takbirs are obligatory, so he observes... but we say that ruku' resembles standing, and based on this resemblance the being missed does not occur, so he performs them in ruku' out of caution. And all these categories are realized in the rights of people: handing over the actual usurped slave is complete performance, and returning him occupied with debt or with a crime due to a cause that occurred in the hand of the usurer is deficient performance. If he gave as dower a slave belonging to another then bought him, his handing over is performance such that she is forced to accept it, meaning the wife, and it is similar to substitute in that he is his owner before delivery so his manumission of him is valid and hers is not. [Some text] until possibility. So raising the hands in the takbirs is sunna, and likewise placing them on the knees in ruku' is sunna, so one should not leave one for the other. And this is analogous to the substitute that resembles performance because this is substitute in essence as its place is standing before ruku' and it was missed, but it resembles performance as the author explained. It resembles standing because the lower half remains as it is, and because one who catches the Imam in ruku' has caught the rak'ah with all its parts of standing and recitation virtually. When he finished explaining the types of performance and substitute in the rights of Allah, he began explaining their types in the rights of people. And these seven types mentioned of performance and substitute are all realized etc. also as they are realized in the rights of Allah. The usurped slave in the description upon which the usurpation occurred: complete performance because it is a performance as it was usurped in its original state and description, so it is like performing prayer in congregation in the rights of Allah. And returning him occupied etc.: meaning returning the usurped slave occupied with debt or with a crime: if the slave consumed the property of a person while in the hand of the usurer so debt becomes attached to his neck, or he committed a crime that deserves his neck or limb while in the hand of the usurer, then returning that slave is deficient performance. As for it being performance, it is apparent because it is returning that slave that was the object of usurpation. As for it being deficient, it is due to deficiency in description where he returned him in a different description from that upon which the usurpation occurred, and it becomes like performing prayer individually. So if that slave perishes in the hand of the owner before handing him to the guardian of the crime, or sale for the debt, the usurer becomes free from liability because the original performance existed. If he handed him to the guardian of the crime or he was killed in it, or sold for that debt, the owner has recourse against the usurer for the value of the slave due to deficiency in performance, as if it did not exist. Returning his delivery to the wife in the dower is performance and similar to substitute etc.: this is analogous to the performance that resembles substitute. The summary: if a man marries a woman and makes her dower a specific slave owned by someone else, then he buys that slave and delivers him to his wife, that is performance, because he delivered what was contracted, such that the woman is forced to accept that slave as dower, and this is a sign of it being performance and similar to substitute.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on the types of adā' (performance) and qadā' (substitute performance) in both divine and human rights. The author begins with a discussion about the ruling on charity after the days of sacrifice (udhiya). He explains that if someone does not sacrifice during the prescribed days, he must give charity of the sheep or its value, not by qiyas (analogy) to sacrifice, but as a return to the original principle: charity is the foundation in matters of wealth. Sacrifice is a divinely ordained act not fully rationalized, so it cannot be extended by qiyas. Instead, the ruling is based on istihsan and caution. Then he supports this with an example from the Eid prayer: if someone joins the imam in ruku', according to Abu Yusuf he does not say the takbīrāt because he missed their place (standing), but the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) says he says them in ruku' because ruku' resembles standing, so the takbīrāt are not truly missed. This illustrates the principle that what is not rationally analogous cannot have a substitute, but if there is a resemblance, it may be performed out of caution. The passage then moves to rights of people. It categorizes returns of usurped property: returning a slave in the same condition as when usurped is complete performance (adā' kāmil), while returning him with a debt or crime attached is deficient performance (adā' qāṣir). Similarly, giving a dower (mahr) of a slave owned by another, then buying it and delivering it, is considered adā' (performance) because the husband delivers what was contracted; it is also similar to qadā' because he acquires ownership only before delivery. The author emphasizes that these categories mirror those in divine rights, showing a systematic application of usul principles across different areas of fiqh.

Key Terms
أداء (adā'): Performance of an obligation at its proper time and in its proper form, without deficiency.
قضاء (qadā'): Substitute performance of an obligation after its proper time, or performing a similar act when the original is impossible.
تضحية (udhiya): Sacrifice of an animal during the days of Eid al-Adha as an act of worship.
غیر معقول (ghayr ma'qūl): An act whose legal cause (illa) is not rationally comprehensible, such as devotional acts (ta'abbudi).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do who joined the Imam in ruku' during Eid prayer?
A) He should not say the takbīrāt at all.
B) He should say the takbīrāt with raising hands in ruku'.
C) He should say the takbīrāt without raising hands in ruku'.
D) He should make up the takbīrāt after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that non-rational devotional acts are not extended by qiyas; instead, after their time, the ruling reverts to the original principle (e.g., charity). In parallel, obligations can be fulfilled in resembling postures out of caution, as in the takbīrāt in ruku'.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Ada' Kamil and Ada' Qasir in Huquq al-Ibad
Commentary on categories of ada' and qada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between complete performance (ada' kamil) and deficient performance (ada' qasir) in huquq al-ibad using the usurped slave example.

Core Idea
Delivering the exact usurped item is complete ada'; returning it encumbered is deficient ada' due to change in quality.

This lesson explores how the categories of ada' (performance) apply to rights of people. The commentary uses the example of a usurped slave to illustrate that ada' is graded: returning the slave as is constitutes complete performance, but returning him encumbered with a debt or crime incurred during usurpation is deficient because the quality has changed. Understanding this distinction helps in evaluating when obligations are truly fulfilled in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its categories
What are the two types of ada' discussed? The text mentions 'ada' kamil' (complete) and 'ada' qasir' (deficient).
2
Locate the example
How is the usurped slave used? The slave is returned exactly as taken (complete) or returned with a debt/crime attached (deficient).
3
Understand the basis for classification
What makes one complete and the other deficient? Complete: the slave is returned in the same condition. Deficient: the slave's quality changed due to the debt/crime.
4
Trace the analogy to rights of Allah
How does this parallel prayer? Complete ada' is like prayer in congregation; deficient is like prayer alone.
The analogy helps in grasping the concept.

لكنا نقول بأن الركوع يشبه القيام فباعتبار هذه الشبهة لايتحقق الفوات، فيؤتى أي المشابهة بها في الركوع احتياطاً. وهذه الأقسام كلها تتحقق في حقوق العباد، فتسليم عين العبد المغصوب أداء كامل ورده مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بسبب كان في يد الغاصب أداء قاصر. وإذا أمهر عبد الغير ثم اشتراه كان تسليمه أداء وشبيها بالقضاء من حيث إنه مملوكه قبل التسليم حتى ينفذ إعتاقه فيه دون إعتاقها، حالهما حتى الإمكان، فرفع اليدين في التكبيرات سنة، وكذا وضعهما على الركبتين في الركوع سنة، فلا يترك أحدهما بالآخر، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي هو شبيه بالأداء؛ لأن هذا قضاء من حيث الذات؛ لأن محلّها القيام قبل الركوع وقد فات لكنه شبيه بالأداء كما بينه المصنف. يشبه القيام لقيام النصف الأسفل على حاله، ولأن من أدرك الإمام في الركوع فقد أدرك الركعة بجميع أجزائها من القيام والقراءة تقديراً. ولما فرغ من بيان أنواع الأداء والقضاء في حقوق الله تعالى شرع في بيان أنواعهما في حقوق العباد. وهذه الأقسام السبعة المذكورة من الأداء والقضاء. كلها تتحقق إلخ أيضا كما تتحقق في حقوق الله تعالى. العبد المغصوب على الوصف الذي ورد عليه الغصب. أداء كامل لأنه أداء كما غصب من الأصل والوصف، فكان كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة في حقوق الله تعالى. ورده مشغولاً إلخ: يعنى ردّ العبد المغصوب مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بأن استهلك العبد مال إنسان حال كونه في يد الغاصب فتعلّق برقبته الدين، أو جنى جناية يستحق بها رقبته أو طرفه حال كونه في يد الغاصب، فردّ ذلك العبد أداء قاصر، أما كونه أداء فظاهر لرد ذلك العبد الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وأما كونه قاصراً فلقصور في الوصف حيث ردّه على غير الوصف الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وصار كأداء الصلاة منفرداً، فلو هلك ذلك العبد في يد المالك قبل الدفع إلى ولي الجناية، أو البيع في الدين برئ الغاصب لوجود أصل الأداء، ولو دفع إلى ولي الجناية أو قتل فيها، أو بيع في ذلك الدين المالك على الغاصب بقيمة العبد لقصور في الأداء، فكأنه لم يوجد. رجع تسليمه إلى الزوجة في المهر أداء وشبيها بالقضاء إلخ: هذا نظير للأداء الشبيه بالقضاء. وحاصله إذا تزوج الرجل بامرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً معيّنا مملوكا لغيره، ثم اشترى ذلك العبد وسلّمه إلى زوجته كان ذلك أداء، حيث سلّم ما وقع عليه العقد حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول ذلك العبد الممهور، وهذا من علامة كونه أداء وشبيها بالقضاء؛ لأن العبد إذا كان في ملك سيّده كان شخصاً آخر، ثم إذا اشتراه الزوج كان شخصا آخر، وإذا سلّمه إليها كان شخصا آخر؛ وذلك لأن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، والدليل في ذلك ما رواه الشيخان عن عائشة لما قالت: دخل رسول الله والبرمة تفور بلحم، فقرب إليه خبز وأدم من أدم البيت فقال: ألم أربُرمةً فيها لحم؟ قالوا: بلى، ولكن ذلك لحم تُصدّق به على بريرة وأنت لا تأكل الصدقة، قال: "هو عليها صدقة ولنا هدية". [البخاري، رقم: ٥۰۹۷] فعلم أن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، فكان الزوج لم يسلّم إليها ما وقع عليه العقد، بل سلّم إليها غيره؛ لأنه قبل التسليم كان مملوكاً للزوج، وتبدل الملك العين حكما كما عرفت ولهذا ينفذ إعتاق الزوج إياه؛ لأنه مملوكه ولا ينفذ إعتاق المرأة فيه قبل التسليم إليها. وهذا مثمرة كونه شبيهاً بالقضاء، ولما كانت ذات العبد موجودة في الحالين ووصف المملوكية متغيّر فيهما جعل أداء شبيها بالقضاء نظراً إلى الذات، ولم يجعل العكس. ولما فرغ عن أنواع الأداء شرع في أنواع القضاء. وضمان الغصب : أي الشيء المغصوب بالمثل فيما إذا غصب مثليا واستهلكه ووجد المثل فيما بين الناس أو بالقيمة فيما لم يكن له مثل أو كان له مثل ولكن انصرم عن أيدي الناس. قضاء بمثل معقول: أما الأول فظاهر؛ لكونه مثلا صورةً ومعنى، وأما الثاني فهو مثل معنى وإن لم يكن صورةً فالأول كامل، والثاني قاصر، فهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل معقول مع تسميه غير معقول: إذ لا مماثلة بين الفائت من النفس والأطراف وبين المال، أما صورة فظاهر، وأما معنى فلأن المال مملوك والآدمي مالك، وإنما شرع الله الدية لئلا تهدر النفس المحترمة مجاناً، وهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل غير معقول تسليمه أي الزوج القيمة إلى المرأة. بالمسمّى وهو العبد المتوسط تجبر على القبول فكذا تجبر على قبول القيمة، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي في معنى الأداء. وحاصله إذا تزوّج الرجل امرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً غير معين بأن قال: نكحتك على عبد، فصحت التسمية عندنا خلافا للشافعي، فحينئذ إن اشترى عبداً وسطاً وسلّمه إليها كان أداء، وإن أتاها قيمة عبد وسط كان قضاء؛ إذ هو تسليم مثل الواجب ولكنه في معنى الأداء؛ إذ العبد هنا مجهول الوصف لا يمكن تسليمه، إلا بأن يسلّم عبداً وسطاً، والوسط لا يتحقق بغير التقويم، فصارت القيمة أصلا بهذا الوجه، فكان تسليم القيمة مثل تسليم العبد الوسط، فكان أداء من هذا الوجه حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول القسمة، كما تجبر على قبول عبد وسط بخلاف العبد المعين والمكيل والموزون الموصوف؛ لأن المسمّى معلوم جنساً ووصفا، فكانت قيمته قضاء خالصاً.
But we say that bowing (ruku') resembles standing (qiyam); by virtue of this resemblance, expiration (fawat) does not occur, so the resembling action is performed in bowing as a precaution. And all these categories occur in the rights of people (huquq al-ibad). So delivering the exact usurped slave is complete performance (ada' kamil), and returning him encumbered with a debt or a crime that occurred while in the usurper's hand is deficient performance (ada' qasir). And if he makes as mahr a slave owned by another, then purchases him, his delivery is performance that resembles compensation (qada') in that it is his property before delivery, such that his manumission of it is valid but not hers. So raising the hands in the takbirs is sunnah, similarly placing them on the knees in bowing is sunnah, so one is not abandoned for the other. And this is analogous to qada' that resembles ada'; for this is qada' in essence because its place is standing before bowing and it has expired, but it resembles ada' as the author explained. It resembles standing by the lower half remaining in place, and because whoever catches the imam in bowing has caught the rak'ah with all its parts of standing and recitation virtually. Having finished explaining the types of ada' and qada' in the rights of Allah, he began explaining their types in the rights of people. And these seven mentioned categories of ada' and qada' all occur, etc., just as they occur in the rights of Allah. The usurped slave in the condition in which the usurpation occurred is complete ada' because it is delivered as it was taken in origin and quality, so it is like performing prayer in congregation in the rights of Allah. And his return encumbered, etc.: meaning the return of the usurped slave encumbered with a debt or a crime, such that the slave consumed someone's property while in the usurper's hand, so a debt attached to his neck, or he committed a crime deserving his neck or limb while in the usurper's hand, so returning such a slave is deficient ada'. As for it being ada', it is clear because he returns the very slave that was usurped. As for it being deficient, it is due to deficiency in quality because he returns him in a different quality from that on which the usurpation occurred, and it is like performing prayer alone. If that slave perishes in the owner's hand before delivery to the guardian of the crime, or is sold for the debt, the usurper is discharged because the basis of ada' exists. If he delivers him to the guardian of the crime, or is killed thereby, or sold for that debt, the owner has recourse against the usurper for the value of the slave due to deficiency in ada', as if it did not occur. His delivery to the wife in the mahr is ada' that resembles qada', etc. This is analogous to ada' that resembles qada'. Its summary: if a man marries a woman and makes as her mahr a specific slave owned by another, then purchases that slave and delivers him to his wife, that is ada', because he delivered what was contracted upon, so the woman is compelled to accept that slave as mahr, and this is a sign of it being ada' that resembles qada'. Because the slave when owned by his master was a different entity, then when the husband purchased him he became another entity, and when he delivered him to her he became another entity. That is because change of ownership legally causes change of substance. The evidence for this is what the two shaykhs narrated from 'A'isha when she said: The Messenger of Allah entered while the pot was boiling with meat, and bread and condiment from the household were brought near, and he said: "Didn't I see a pot with meat?" They said: Yes, but that meat was given in charity to Barirah, and you do not eat charity. He said: "It is charity for her and a gift for us." Thus it is known that change of ownership legally causes change of substance. So the husband did not deliver to her what was contracted upon, but delivered something else, because before delivery it was owned by the husband, and change of ownership legally changes the substance as you have learned. Hence the husband's manumission of it is valid because it is his property, but the wife's manumission of it before delivery to her is not valid. This is the fruit of it being resembling qada'. Since the slave's essence exists in both states and the attribute of ownership changes, it was made ada' resembling qada' in consideration of the essence, and not the opposite. Having finished the types of ada', he began the types of qada'. And guaranty of usurpation: i.e., the usurped thing by an equivalent (mithl) if he usurped a like item (mithli) and consumed it and the equivalent is found among people, or by value if it has no equivalent or has an equivalent but has disappeared from people's hands. It is qada' with a rational equivalent (mithl ma'qul). As for the first, it is clear because it is an equivalent in form and meaning. As for the second, it is an equivalent in meaning though not in form; the first is complete, the second deficient. So this is analogous to qada' with a rational equivalent. And its being called non-rational: because there is no similarity between the lost life/limb and property—as for form it is obvious, as for meaning because property is owned while the human is an owner. Allah legislated blood-money (diyah) so that the respected soul is not wasted in vain. This is analogous to qada' with a non-rational equivalent. His delivery (the husband's) of the value to the woman. By the named (musamma) which is the average slave, she is compelled to accept; likewise she is compelled to accept the value. And this is analogous to qada' that is in the meaning of ada'. Its summary: if a man marries a woman and makes her mahr an unspecified slave by saying: "I marry you upon a slave," the naming is valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Then if he purchases an average slave and delivers him to her, it is ada'. If he gives her the value of an average slave, it is qada', because it is delivery of the equivalent of what is obligatory, but it is in the meaning of ada'. Because the slave here is unspecified in description and cannot be delivered except by delivering an average slave, and the average cannot be determined without valuation, so the value becomes a basis in this regard. So delivering the value is like delivering the average slave, so it is ada' from this aspect, such that the woman is compelled to accept the valuation, just as she is compelled to accept an average slave. This is unlike the specified slave or weighed/measured items described, because the named item is known in genus and description, so its value is pure qada'.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of ada' (performance) and qada' (compensation) as they apply to rights of people (huquq al-ibad). The author begins by drawing an analogy from prayer (rights of Allah) to clarify the categories: full ada' (like performing an act exactly as required), deficient ada' (like performing an act with a flaw), and ada' that resembles qada' (like performing an act that in essence is compensation but is considered performance due to resemblance). Using the example of a usurped slave, he explains that returning the slave as is constitutes full ada', while returning him encumbered with debts or crimes incurred during the usurpation is deficient ada'. The commentary then discusses a marriage case where the mahr is a slave owned by another; if the husband later purchases and delivers that slave, it is ada' resembling qada' because ownership change legally transforms the entity. This is supported by the hadith of Barirah, where the Prophet accepted meat as a gift that had been charity for Barirah, illustrating that change of ownership changes the legal status of the object. The passage then addresses qada' in two forms: with a rational equivalent (like paying an exact replacement for a usurped item) and with a non-rational equivalent (like diyah for life or limb, which cannot truly be replaced by money but is legislated to prevent disregard). Finally, it discusses a marriage with an unspecified slave as mahr: according to the Hanafi school (contrary to al-Shafi'i), the naming is valid; delivering an average slave is ada', but paying its value is qada' that is in the meaning of ada' because the unspecified nature makes valuation essential. The commentary maintains a Hanafi perspective throughout, emphasizing the role of analogy (qiyas) and legal reasoning (istihsan) in deriving these rulings.

Key Terms
أداء (ada'): Performance of an obligation exactly as required, such as delivering the very object that was usurped or performing prayer in congregation.
قضاء (qada'): Compensation for a missed or lost obligation, such as paying the value of a consumed item or paying diyah for life.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the usurped slave, what makes the return 'deficient ada''?
A) The slave is not returned at all
B) The slave is returned with a debt or crime attached
C) The slave is returned to the wrong person
D) The slave is returned after a long delay

Key Takeaway
Ada' in huquq al-ibad is classified as complete or deficient based on whether the obligation is fulfilled in its original quality, not merely by delivering the same physical object.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
10 min
Ada' Resembling Qada': The Tabaddul al-Milk Principle
Commentary explaining a specific category of ada' resembling qada' using mahr case and hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why delivering a purchased slave as mahr is considered ada' resembling qada', and apply the principle that change of ownership legally changes the substance (tabaddul al-milk).

Core Idea
Change of ownership legally transforms the same object, making its delivery ada' resembling qada'.

This lesson examines a fascinating category: ada' that resembles qada'. The example involves a husband who makes a slave owned by another as mahr, then purchases and delivers it. The commentary explains that because ownership changed, the slave is legally a different entity, so the delivery is ada' in form but resembles qada' in substance. The supporting evidence is the hadith of Barirah, where the Prophet accepted charity meat as a gift after ownership changed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
What is the scenario? Husband marries woman, mahr = specific slave owned by another, then husband buys that slave and delivers it.
2
Classify the delivery
How is this delivery classified? It is ada' resembling qada' (ada' shabih bil-qada').
3
Understand the reasoning
Why does it resemble qada'? Because the slave, when owned by the husband before delivery, is legally a different entity than when belonging to the original owner. Change of ownership (tabaddul al-milk) causes a change in legal substance.
4
Examine the evidence
What is the dalil? The hadith of Barirah: charity meat becomes a gift for the Prophet after ownership changes.
5
Note the legal effect
What practical consequence follows? The husband can manumit the slave after delivery, but the wife cannot before delivery.

لكنا نقول بأن الركوع يشبه القيام فباعتبار هذه الشبهة لايتحقق الفوات، فيؤتى أي المشابهة بها في الركوع احتياطاً. وهذه الأقسام كلها تتحقق في حقوق العباد، فتسليم عين العبد المغصوب أداء كامل ورده مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بسبب كان في يد الغاصب أداء قاصر. وإذا أمهر عبد الغير ثم اشتراه كان تسليمه أداء وشبيها بالقضاء من حيث إنه مملوكه قبل التسليم حتى ينفذ إعتاقه فيه دون إعتاقها، حالهما حتى الإمكان، فرفع اليدين في التكبيرات سنة، وكذا وضعهما على الركبتين في الركوع سنة، فلا يترك أحدهما بالآخر، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي هو شبيه بالأداء؛ لأن هذا قضاء من حيث الذات؛ لأن محلّها القيام قبل الركوع وقد فات لكنه شبيه بالأداء كما بينه المصنف. يشبه القيام لقيام النصف الأسفل على حاله، ولأن من أدرك الإمام في الركوع فقد أدرك الركعة بجميع أجزائها من القيام والقراءة تقديراً. ولما فرغ من بيان أنواع الأداء والقضاء في حقوق الله تعالى شرع في بيان أنواعهما في حقوق العباد. وهذه الأقسام السبعة المذكورة من الأداء والقضاء. كلها تتحقق إلخ أيضا كما تتحقق في حقوق الله تعالى. العبد المغصوب على الوصف الذي ورد عليه الغصب. أداء كامل لأنه أداء كما غصب من الأصل والوصف، فكان كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة في حقوق الله تعالى. ورده مشغولاً إلخ: يعنى ردّ العبد المغصوب مشغولاً بالدين أو بالجناية بأن استهلك العبد مال إنسان حال كونه في يد الغاصب فتعلّق برقبته الدين، أو جنى جناية يستحق بها رقبته أو طرفه حال كونه في يد الغاصب، فردّ ذلك العبد أداء قاصر، أما كونه أداء فظاهر لرد ذلك العبد الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وأما كونه قاصراً فلقصور في الوصف حيث ردّه على غير الوصف الذي وقع عليه الغصب، وصار كأداء الصلاة منفرداً، فلو هلك ذلك العبد في يد المالك قبل الدفع إلى ولي الجناية، أو البيع في الدين برئ الغاصب لوجود أصل الأداء، ولو دفع إلى ولي الجناية أو قتل فيها، أو بيع في ذلك الدين المالك على الغاصب بقيمة العبد لقصور في الأداء، فكأنه لم يوجد. رجع تسليمه إلى الزوجة في المهر أداء وشبيها بالقضاء إلخ: هذا نظير للأداء الشبيه بالقضاء. وحاصله إذا تزوج الرجل بامرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً معيّنا مملوكا لغيره، ثم اشترى ذلك العبد وسلّمه إلى زوجته كان ذلك أداء، حيث سلّم ما وقع عليه العقد حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول ذلك العبد الممهور، وهذا من علامة كونه أداء وشبيها بالقضاء؛ لأن العبد إذا كان في ملك سيّده كان شخصاً آخر، ثم إذا اشتراه الزوج كان شخصا آخر، وإذا سلّمه إليها كان شخصا آخر؛ وذلك لأن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، والدليل في ذلك ما رواه الشيخان عن عائشة لما قالت: دخل رسول الله والبرمة تفور بلحم، فقرب إليه خبز وأدم من أدم البيت فقال: ألم أربُرمةً فيها لحم؟ قالوا: بلى، ولكن ذلك لحم تُصدّق به على بريرة وأنت لا تأكل الصدقة، قال: "هو عليها صدقة ولنا هدية". [البخاري، رقم: ٥۰۹۷] فعلم أن تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً، فكان الزوج لم يسلّم إليها ما وقع عليه العقد، بل سلّم إليها غيره؛ لأنه قبل التسليم كان مملوكاً للزوج، وتبدل الملك العين حكما كما عرفت ولهذا ينفذ إعتاق الزوج إياه؛ لأنه مملوكه ولا ينفذ إعتاق المرأة فيه قبل التسليم إليها. وهذا مثمرة كونه شبيهاً بالقضاء، ولما كانت ذات العبد موجودة في الحالين ووصف المملوكية متغيّر فيهما جعل أداء شبيها بالقضاء نظراً إلى الذات، ولم يجعل العكس. ولما فرغ عن أنواع الأداء شرع في أنواع القضاء. وضمان الغصب : أي الشيء المغصوب بالمثل فيما إذا غصب مثليا واستهلكه ووجد المثل فيما بين الناس أو بالقيمة فيما لم يكن له مثل أو كان له مثل ولكن انصرم عن أيدي الناس. قضاء بمثل معقول: أما الأول فظاهر؛ لكونه مثلا صورةً ومعنى، وأما الثاني فهو مثل معنى وإن لم يكن صورةً فالأول كامل، والثاني قاصر، فهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل معقول مع تسميه غير معقول: إذ لا مماثلة بين الفائت من النفس والأطراف وبين المال، أما صورة فظاهر، وأما معنى فلأن المال مملوك والآدمي مالك، وإنما شرع الله الدية لئلا تهدر النفس المحترمة مجاناً، وهذا نظير للقضاء بمثل غير معقول تسليمه أي الزوج القيمة إلى المرأة. بالمسمّى وهو العبد المتوسط تجبر على القبول فكذا تجبر على قبول القيمة، وهذا نظير للقضاء الذي في معنى الأداء. وحاصله إذا تزوّج الرجل امرأة وجعل مهرها عبداً غير معين بأن قال: نكحتك على عبد، فصحت التسمية عندنا خلافا للشافعي، فحينئذ إن اشترى عبداً وسطاً وسلّمه إليها كان أداء، وإن أتاها قيمة عبد وسط كان قضاء؛ إذ هو تسليم مثل الواجب ولكنه في معنى الأداء؛ إذ العبد هنا مجهول الوصف لا يمكن تسليمه، إلا بأن يسلّم عبداً وسطاً، والوسط لا يتحقق بغير التقويم، فصارت القيمة أصلا بهذا الوجه، فكان تسليم القيمة مثل تسليم العبد الوسط، فكان أداء من هذا الوجه حتى تجبر المرأة على قبول القسمة، كما تجبر على قبول عبد وسط بخلاف العبد المعين والمكيل والموزون الموصوف؛ لأن المسمّى معلوم جنساً ووصفا، فكانت قيمته قضاء خالصاً.

The evidence for this is what the two shaykhs narrated from 'A'isha when she said: The Messenger of Allah entered while the pot was boiling with meat, and bread and condiment from the household were brought near, and he said: "Didn't I see a pot with meat?" They said: Yes, but that meat was given in charity to Barirah, and you do not eat charity. He said: "It is charity for her and a gift for us." Thus it is known that change of ownership legally causes change of substance. So the husband did not deliver to her what was contracted upon, but delivered something else, because before delivery it was owned by the husband, and change of ownership legally changes the substance as you have learned. Hence the husband's manumission of it is valid because it is his property, but the wife's manumission of it before delivery to her is not valid. This is the fruit of it being resembling qada'. Since the slave's essence exists in both states and the attribute of ownership changes, it was made ada' resembling qada' in consideration of the essence, and not the opposite. Having finished the types of ada', he began the types of qada'. And guaranty of usurpation: i.e., the usurped thing by an equivalent (mithl) if he usurped a like item (mithli) and consumed it and the equivalent is found among people, or by value if it has no equivalent or has an equivalent but has disappeared from people's hands. It is qada' with a rational equivalent (mithl ma'qul). As for the first, it is clear because it is an equivalent in form and meaning. As for the second, it is an equivalent in meaning though not in form; the first is complete, the second deficient. So this is analogous to qada' with a rational equivalent. And its being called non-rational: because there is no similarity between the lost life/limb and property—as for form it is obvious, as for meaning because property is owned while the human is an owner. Allah legislated blood-money (diyah) so that the respected soul is not wasted in vain. This is analogous to qada' with a non-rational equivalent. His delivery (the husband's) of the value to the woman. By the named (musamma) which is the average slave, she is compelled to accept; likewise she is compelled to accept the value. And this is analogous to qada' that is in the meaning of ada'. Its summary: if a man marries a woman and makes her mahr an unspecified slave by saying: "I marry you upon a slave," the naming is valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i. Then if he purchases an average slave and delivers him to her, it is ada'. If he gives her the value of an average slave, it is qada', because it is delivery of the equivalent of what is obligatory, but it is in the meaning of ada'. Because the slave here is unspecified in description and cannot be delivered except by delivering an average slave, and the average cannot be determined without valuation, so the value becomes a basis in this regard. So delivering the value is like delivering the average slave, so it is ada' from this aspect, such that the woman is compelled to accept the valuation, just as she is compelled to accept an average slave. This is unlike the specified slave or weighed/measured items described, because the named item is known in genus and description, so its value is pure qada'.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of ada' (performance) and qada' (compensation) as they apply to rights of people (huquq al-ibad). The author begins by drawing an analogy from prayer (rights of Allah) to clarify the categories: full ada' (like performing an act exactly as required), deficient ada' (like performing an act with a flaw), and ada' that resembles qada' (like performing an act that in essence is compensation but is considered performance due to resemblance). Using the example of a usurped slave, he explains that returning the slave as is constitutes full ada', while returning him encumbered with debts or crimes incurred during the usurpation is deficient ada'. The commentary then discusses a marriage case where the mahr is a slave owned by another; if the husband later purchases and delivers that slave, it is ada' resembling qada' because ownership change legally transforms the entity. This is supported by the hadith of Barirah, where the Prophet accepted meat as a gift that had been charity for Barirah, illustrating that change of ownership changes the legal status of the object. The passage then addresses qada' in two forms: with a rational equivalent (like paying an exact replacement for a usurped item) and with a non-rational equivalent (like diyah for life or limb, which cannot truly be replaced by money but is legislated to prevent disregard). Finally, it discusses a marriage with an unspecified slave as mahr: according to the Hanafi school (contrary to al-Shafi'i), the naming is valid; delivering an average slave is ada', but paying its value is qada' that is in the meaning of ada' because the unspecified nature makes valuation essential. The commentary maintains a Hanafi perspective throughout, emphasizing the role of analogy (qiyas) and legal reasoning (istihsan) in deriving these rulings.

Key Terms
تبدل الملك يوجب تبدل العين حكماً (tabaddul al-milk yujibu tabaddul al-'ayn hukman): Change of ownership legally causes change of the substance, so the same object is treated as different after transfer of ownership.
أداء شبيه بالقضاء (ada' shabih bil-qada'): Performance that resembles compensation; the act is ada' in essence but qada' in consideration of ownership change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the evidence cited for the principle 'tabaddul al-milk yujibu tabaddul al-'ayn hukman'?
A) Quranic verse on inheritance
B) Hadith of Barirah about meat
C) Ijma of the Companions
D) Qiyas on prayer

Key Takeaway
Change of ownership can legally transform an object, so delivering an object after ownership change is ada' that resembles qada'.

Qada' with Equivalent and the Unspecified Mahr Dispute
Commentary on types of qada' and a madhhab dispute regarding unspecified mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada' with a rational equivalent (mithl ma'qul) and qada' with a non-rational equivalent (mithl ghayr ma'qul), and explain the Hanafi position on unspecified slave mahr against the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Qada' with a rational equivalent compensates with something similar in form and meaning; with non-rational, only in meaning.

This lesson covers the types of qada' (compensation) in huquq al-ibad. The commentary distinguishes qada' with a rational equivalent (like paying the exact replacement for usurped goods) from qada' with a non-rational equivalent (like diyah for life). It then discusses a dispute with al-Shafi'i over the validity of naming an unspecified slave as mahr. According to Hanafis, the naming is valid and the wife can be compelled to accept a value or an average slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of qada'
Two types: qada' with rational equivalent (mithl ma'qul) and with non-rational equivalent (mithl ghayr ma'qul).
2
Understand the first type
Paying the exact equivalent for usurped mithli goods: same in form and meaning.
3
Understand the second type
Paying diyah for life/limb: no true similarity in form, only in meaning (to prevent loss).
4
Analyze the unspecified slave mahr dispute
Hanafi: naming is valid, wife can be compelled to accept average slave or its value. Shafi'i: naming invalid due to ambiguity.
5
Apply the qada' categories to the dispute
Paying value for unspecified slave is qada' that is in the meaning of ada'.
